Respectfully, I invoke the presence of the Directing Envoy of the Orthodox Unity, the Merit Officers of the Celestial Bureaus, the Tiger-Rushing Guardians of the Central Office—two each from the Five Hundreds—and twelve Commandants. Further, five each of the Merit Officers, Scribes, Assistants, Lesser Clerks, and Golden Radiance Lads; two each of the Supervisors of the Central Registers, Couriers, and Attendant Envoys. May they all simultaneously oversee the proceedings, jointly examine and verify, burn away the old and dust-laden, and receive the radiance of the new, thereby pardoning this servant’s foolish shortcomings and inadvertent transgressions.

May the previously printed and transcribed memorials ascend forever to the Celestial Archives, and may all subsequently submitted petitions be spared the Cold Pond. Let the assembled officials bear witness, rewarding and aiding those who have rendered service, in accordance with the statutes governing merit and without betraying the trust of efficacy.

I humbly beseech the Most High to discern and heed this plea.

The number of severed memorials varies, for times differ in abundance and restraint, and the law adapts to action or concealment. When concealed, fewer are required; when enacted, more. The tally is completed upon reaching one hundred memorials for severance. As stated earlier, each year’s severance concludes in the tenth month.

**Memorials and Cases**
The case for memorials shall measure two feet four inches in length, one foot two inches in width, and eight inches in height, and must feature curved legs. Nanmu or catalpa wood is preferred. Modern use of tall, straight-legged cases is contrary to the statutes and will result in the forfeiture of one’s allotted years.

**The Heavenly Elder Questions the Three Sovereigns**
The Heavenly Elder questioned the Three Sovereigns: “Why are talismans made on *wuxu* days?”

The Three Sovereigns replied: “*Xu* is the Gate of Heaven. *Wu* is the likeness of the Earth’s Central Office and its Lord. The Heavenly Thearch customarily descends from the Gate of Heaven to wander on *wuxu* days. When talismans are crafted on this day, he rejoices and bestows the fulfillment of wishes. *Wu* pertains to earth; thus, one is certain to attain official rank, be enfeoffed as a marquis, and receive a domain.”

They are to be worn at the hour of *wu*, for *wu* embodies the essence of the Great Yang and the radiance of pure metal—an emblem of lofty rank and golden-purple eminence.

**Avoidances and Taboos**

**Regulations and Prohibitions**

The Regulations state: When submitting memorials or performing *jiao* rites, disciples must not take life. Violations reduce one’s allotted years by twenty-four.

When submitting memorials, all members of the household, including fowl and dogs, must not create clamor. Violations incur a penalty of twelve years’ reduction.

Memorials must not be submitted during great winds, heavy rains, or prolonged storms. Violations result in one year of illness.

Those afflicted with the six ailments must not submit memorials on behalf of others. Violations reduce one’s allotted years by thirty-six.

When submitting memorials, one must not consume wine, meat, or the five pungent vegetables. Violations reduce one’s allotted years by twelve.

**Prohibitions**

The Prohibitions state: When submitting memorials in the offices of the Dao to request official appointments, one must not transgress or err. Those defiled by impurity must not enter the ritual space.

Those who have witnessed a burial must not enter rivers, mountains, marshes, or forests. Livestock that have given birth within seven days must not enter the ritual space. Infants under one hundred days old must not enter the ritual space. Livestock that have borne young within a month must not enter the ritual space.

Objects of faith used in memorials and *jiao* rites must not be lent to others. Within the ritual space, one must not burn foul or odorous substances, nor feathers, hides, or horns.

All who enter the ritual space must do so with reverence and solemnity, performing rites of obeisance. One must not act with arrogance or irreverence.

Within the ritual space, one must not point or gesture, speak recklessly or unlawfully, or engage in frivolous speech or laughter. One must not expose the body.

Offerings of faith must be distributed among the Daoist faithful.

When approaching the ritual space to submit memorials for the salvation of the sick or the alleviation of misfortune, one must don a sash, wear wooden clogs, and bow respectfully, knocking one’s head to the ground while recounting the matter in full. One must not act with arrogance, cruelty, or haughtiness, nor raise one’s voice in self-aggrandizement. Violations are judged under the three penalties.

The Decrees state: If a father is afflicted with illness or misfortune while his son bears the great register of the Celestial Master, the father must don a cap and hempen robe, knock his head to the ground, and strike his cheeks. Only then may the son enter the ritual space to submit the memorial.

The Decrees state: If father and son seek to make requests improperly, both father and son are judged under the three penalties. The same applies to brothers.

The Decrees state: If a woman holds a register of the Dao and her husband faces urgent misfortune, he must don a sash, wear wooden clogs, and bow respectfully according to the rites. Only then may the woman enter the oratory to submit the memorial.

The Decrees state: If a husband makes a request improperly, he is judged under two penalties. If a wife fails to proclaim the decree clearly, she is judged under three penalties.

The Decrees state: If an uncle or elder male cousin is afflicted with illness or misfortune while a nephew or younger male cousin bears the register, the latter must submit a memorial as in the case of father and son.

The Decrees state: If a mother’s brother or sister is afflicted with illness or misfortune, and their children or grandchildren seek to submit a memorial, they must do so as in the case of uncles and nephews.

The Decrees state: Those who commit heinous acts—wielding the sword to execute, plotting against their lord, or murdering their father—are guilty of great treason. No amount of wealth or merit can atone for such crimes. They shall tread upon the Mountain of Knives, ascend the Forest of Swords, endure the cauldron’s boiling waters, and suffer burning and scalding for ten thousand generations without reprieve, their sins beyond redemption.

**Disciplinary Statutes**

The Disciplinary Statutes state: Within the human body resides a spirit that records transgressions, ascending and descending with the passing of time, daily noting good and evil.

One hundred and twenty transgressions form a *ke*, which brings more harm than benefit. One hundred and eighty transgressions form a *hao*, which causes livestock to fail to reproduce. Ten transgressions form a *bian*, which brings illness. Five hundred and forty transgressions form a *xiong*, which harms the fetus and injures children. Seven hundred and twenty transgressions form a *chui*, which brings death. Seven hundred and twenty-nine transgressions form a *yang*, which causes muteness, paralysis, blindness, or deafness. One thousand and eighty transgressions form a *huo*, which brings sudden, premature death. One thousand two hundred transgressions form a *can*, which produces rebellious offspring. One thousand two hundred and sixty transgressions form a *jiu*, which severs the line of descent. One thousand four hundred transgressions form a *ji*, which brings calamity flowing through five generations. One thousand six hundred and twenty transgressions form a *zhe*, which severs the lineage, leaving no descendants. One thousand eight hundred transgressions form a *huan*, which causes the family to produce those afflicted with madness or idiocy. Two thousand and sixty transgressions form a *bao*, which brings violent death by weapons. Two thousand three hundred and thirty transgressions form a *xu*, which causes family members—father and son, brothers—to attack one another. Two thousand five hundred and twenty transgressions form a *zeng*, which brings severe skin diseases to the family. Two thousand seven hundred transgressions form a *hai*, which causes deafness in the family. Two thousand eight hundred transgressions form a *zai*, which brings familial incest, depravity, and rebellion. Three thousand and sixty transgressions form a *yi*, which causes the family to produce the blind, the castrated, or the mutilated. Three thousand one hundred and thirty transgressions form a *bian*, which brings imprisonment, execution, or the extermination of the clan. Three thousand one hundred and fifty transgressions form a *guai*, which causes the family to produce beggars in the marketplace, their bones discarded and abandoned. Three thousand six hundred transgressions form a *man*, which necessitates death.

The Statutes state: Some die at twenty or thirty, their *ke* filled with misfortune and early death. Others reach fifty or sixty before their *ke* fills with misfortune and early death. Some, though having committed no transgressions in youth, die prematurely—these inherit the residual transgressions of past lives. Others, though committing great evil and treason, live out their years without encountering disaster—they inherit the residual blessings of their ancestors.

Thus, the accumulation of virtue leaves residual fortune, while the accumulation of evil leaves residual misfortune. If one can repent of transgressions, they vanish and fortune arises. One must reflect on one’s faults, take responsibility, reform, and never repeat them. Practicing this for ten days removes one *ke* of transgressions from the spirit within. Practicing for one hundred days removes two *ke*. Practicing for one year removes three *ke*. Practicing for three years brings the corresponding fortune.

If one does not reflect or repent, transgressions deepen daily. Minor transgressions harm only oneself; major transgressions flow down to descendants. Accumulated goodness is like dust upon a beam; accumulated evil is like smoke within a chimney. How can one not be vigilant?

**Auspicious Days for Receiving Registers**

**Auspicious Days for Receiving Registers**

**Days of Righteousness (義日):**
Jiazi, Bingyin, Dingmao, Xinwei, Renshen, Guiyou, Yihai, Bingchen, Xinchou, Dingwei, Gengxu, Wuwu, Gengchen.

**Days of Treasure (寶日):**
Jiawu, Dingchou, Bingxu, Gengzi, Renyin, Dingwei, Wushen, Jiyou, Xinhai, Guimao, Bingchen, Yisi, Bingxu, Bingchen.

**Days of Dedication (專日):**
Jichou, Wuxu, Bingwu, Renzi, Jiayin, Yimao, Jiwei, Gengshen, Xinyou, Guihai, Wuchen, Dingsi, Bingchen, Yiwei.

The above Days of Righteousness, Treasure, and Dedication are auspicious for transmitting and receiving scriptures and registers, and are also recorded in the *Daoist Almanac*.

**Days of Mutual and Self-Punishment (相刑自刑日):**
Zi punishes Mao; Mao punishes Zi. Si punishes Shen; Shen punishes Yin; Yin punishes Si. Wei punishes Chou; Chou punishes Xu; Xu punishes Wei. Chen, Wu, and You are self-punishing. Hai is self-punishing.

These four self-punishing days must be carefully observed in memorials and offerings.

*Red Pine Master’s Memorial Almanac, Scroll Two* (concluded)

*Red Pine Master’s Memorial Almanac*
**Text Title:** *Red Pine Master’s Memorial Almanac*
Author: Unknown; believed to be compiled by Tang-dynasty Daoists. An early liturgical manual for the Heavenly Master Dao tradition.
Six scrolls.
**Source Text:** *Daoist Canon of the Zhengtong Era*, *Dongxuan Section*, *Memorials and Petitions Category*.

*Red Pine Master’s Memorial Almanac, Scroll Three*
**Memorial for Drought** (天旱章)
[Position the ritual implements...]

**Memorial for Drought**

We humbly submit: According to the sacred writ, we, Your servants, though foolish and unworthy, have encountered this Daoist congregation and been blessed to witness this sagely age. By fortunate coincidence, we have been touched by the Great Law. We prostrate ourselves in gratitude to the Most High, whose vast embrace and merciful compassion of the Master Lords have bestowed upon us grace without the slightest merit of our own. Day and night, we tremble with dread, as though treading upon ice or crossing a ravine, unable to repay even a fraction of the恩 of Heaven and Earth.

On the day we received the Law, we vowed to serve the Master’s gate with reverence, to disseminate virtue and power, to assist the state and sustain life, to deliver all beings, and to place salvation of the myriad creatures above all else. Yet of late, the cycles of Heaven and Earth have turned adverse; yin and yang clash; the four seasons lose their proper measure. The realm suffers from severe drought; crops fail to ripen. We fear that demonic calamities will arise in succession: pure yang ascends, congealed yin lingers below; the two qi fail to interact; the mysterious moisture does not descend. Scorching winds and blazing sun afflict the people; crops wither and parch; fish in dried ponds dread the daylight.

This arises because the Son of Heaven, having received the Mandate of Heaven, rules over all domains, yet the Three Talents, the lords and governors, the ministers and local officials have failed to govern with due care, and their administrative achievements fall short. We, Your servants, bear the heavy responsibility of the Dao yet lack the means to propagate its transformative power. Unable to rectify and harmonize the proper sequence of qi, we have caused the Five Phases to lose their balance, inviting the onslaught of celestial disasters.

We have searched the statutes and laws: the qi of the Dao is vast and all-covering, moistening and nourishing all living beings. We have learned that Qian knows the Great Beginning, and Kun brings things to completion. When Heaven and Earth interact in harmony, all things flourish. Spring gives birth, summer nurtures growth, autumn brings harvest, and winter stores away. When yin and yang are harmonious and compliant, grasses and trees flourish, and the Five Grains ripen. The Great Yin governs rain. On the day of *Lichun*, men sow the fields, and women tend to mulberry and hemp, hoping that by autumn and winter they may provide tribute and taxes, sustaining all life under Heaven and upon Earth.

In the second month of *Lichun*, the Five Grains begin to be sown. When rainwater is balanced and harmonious, the Five Grains thrive, and harmonious qi accumulates. Yet for some days now, scorching drought has persisted; sweet rain has not fallen. Yang qi waxes excessive; the sky lacks the impulse to send forth clouds; the earth lacks the moisture of vital fluids. We, Your servants, though unworthy, dare not presume, yet in accordance with the statutes and laws of the Heavenly Master, we venture through boiling waters and scorching fires to humbly submit this memorial. With utmost trepidation and fear, we kowtow, acknowledging our capital offense.

We beseech the Most High, the Boundless Great Dao, the Three Master Lords: You love life and abhor death. We implore You to bestow the transformative power of the Great Dao. May the officials in charge distinguish the Five Phases, regulate the pitch-pipes, array the Eight Trigrams, and mark the months and solar terms, so that yang does not encroach upon its bounds, yin does not retreat from its proper measure. When the Five comes to rest upon the One, Water naturally moistens below; when the Five ascends to the Two, Fire naturally flames upward; when the Five rides upon the Three, Wood naturally bends and straightens; when the Five removes the Four, Metal congeals and transforms; when the Five pairs with itself, the Law nourishes crops. Only when the Five are complete does nothing fail to grow. Then may the *Chunhuo* constellation withdraw its flames, the *Xuanxiao* constellation release its moisture, the *Jisu* constellation pour forth its tongue, the *Bisu* constellation stir its roots. May the coarse stones of the Five Marchmounts and the surging springs of the Four Marshes burst forth.

We humbly implore Your celestial mercy. We reverently request that from the Lingtai Palace, one Han Ming Lord and one hundred twenty officials and generals be dispatched to command the celestial thunder. From the Yuanming Palace, one Xiao Xuan Ming Lord and one hundred twenty officials and generals be dispatched to command Lord Lü, Son of the River Earl; the Thirty-Six Water Emperors; the Twelve Stream Maidens; the Nine River Water Emperors; the subordinate officials of the River Pacification Marquis; and the Water Deities of the Central Region, to summon clouds and send down rain. From the Hetian Palace, one Jiuhai Beixuan Lord and one hundred twenty officials and generals be dispatched to send forth water qi and release wind and thunder. From the Taishan Palace, the Nine Valley Lords of Sizhou and one hundred twenty officials and generals be dispatched to raise water qi. We further request the Nine Sea Lords and Water Emperors of Sizhou, the Envoys of Floating Clouds, and one hundred ten officials and generals to descend together. May they join with the illustrious Earth Lord of this prefecture, county, and township; the spirits of the famous mountains and great marshes, the source-valleys and rivers; the ancient and present ministers and great officials who have rendered service to the people and are enshrined in temples; and all the Perfected Officials of villages, townships, hamlets, and wards. May they register the qi, transmit the talismans, and govern the temple offices. May all the divine lords descend, unite their hearts and strength, assist the Dao of Heaven, perform their numinous powers, summon clouds and send down rain, bestowing abundant moisture and copious soaking. May the parched seedlings receive the glory of fattening moisture; may the myriad people gain the Mandate of renewal.

When the task is accomplished and the affair established, may their merits be reported and their ranks promoted. May the Lords of Wind and Rain likewise ascend to the Three Heavens to receive their due reward. We pray that the Celestial Bureau issue a decree to swiftly cause the drought demons to perish in accordance with this memorial. We specially beseech the Three Masters of the Most High to grant efficacy and verification, that we may not fail in our trust.

May the Most High, in Your discernment, have mercy upon our foolish inadequacy.

We respectfully entrust this to the Direct Envoys of the Two Officials, the Left and Right Official Envoys of the Orthodox Unity Merit Officers, the Scribes of Yin-Yang Divine Formulas, the Charioteers of the Red Talisman Statutes, and the Courier Horses of the Strong Winds, two officials each, to carry forth.

We, Your servants, humbly memorialize on behalf of the parched and desiccated qi of this realm, fearing the failure of the hundred grains. We kowtow and beseech the Celestial Officials to descend in due season, bestowing flowing moisture and abundant soaking.

One precious memorial is hereby submitted to the Three Celestial Bureaus, awaiting Your decree.

We, Your servants, with utmost trepidation and fear, kowtow and bow our heads in reverence, submitting this for Your attention.

---

**Memorial to Cease Rain After Receiving Water**

[Position the ritual implements.]

We humbly submit: According to the sacred writ, we, Your servants, have encountered this turning of the cosmic cycle and been privileged to receive the Master’s Dao, assisting the state and sustaining life. Recently, cold and heat have been unseasonable; demonic afflictions have multiplied. Since the beginning of yang, severe drought has persisted without rain. The people have neglected their agricultural duties; crops wither and parch. We, Your servants, grieve for the people’s distress and have beseeched the descent of clouds and rain. The vast moisture has poured forth in all directions; yin qi has descended without cease. Torrential rains have surged; the hundred rivers overflow. The people have abandoned their livelihoods; fields and seedlings are submerged. The court and the common folk suffer hardship.

We, Your servants, in accordance with ancient rites, humbly submit this memorial, praying that it may be conveyed above. We beseech that the rains be restrained.

We, Your servants, have previously consulted and reported to the Rain and Spring Officials, who have returned to the Heavenly Courts. The Central Officials have recorded and sealed the memorial, advancing to receive merit and reward. We now humbly request one Lord of Righteous Qi of Heaven, along with one hundred and twenty officials and generals, and one thousand two hundred Jade Maidens of the River, each to descend in unison. We beseech the Heavenly Courts to restrain the rains and shift the winds, that the Wind Earl and Rain Master may follow the four seasons and eight solar terms without error, gathering clouds and withdrawing obscuring vapors, so that the Three Luminaries may shine brightly—this being the sign to cease the rains. Let all officials report their merits to receive rewards, thereby demonstrating efficacy and trust.

We implore the Most High to discern and show mercy. As we, Your servants, have received the grace of the throne in our plea for rain, we now beseech its cessation. We humbly submit this memorial, to be conveyed to the [specific] Court. Awaiting the decree, we prostrate ourselves in reverence and awe, bowing our heads to the ground in submission.

---

**Memorial for the Suppression of Locusts, Rats, and Pestilence Devouring Seedlings**

[Your servants] hold their ordained ranks and humbly submit:

We have respectfully examined the records, noting that on such-and-such a day, by fortunate encounter, we were granted the pure transformation of governance. Yet we, Your servants, have repeatedly incurred calamities and faults, and in recent years, our fields and sowings have seldom prospered as desired. This year, in such-and-such a place, the wild grain and planted crops have been devoured by plague locusts, which cannot be restrained. We beseech Your servants to perform exorcism and protection.

Prostrating ourselves, we humbly submit this memorial for Your attention, praying that one Lord of the Heavenly Fields of the Northern Gate, along with one hundred and twenty officials and generals, be dispatched to expel and eliminate all locusts, rats, and creatures that harm and violate the seedlings and crops of our household, causing all such vermin and pests to vanish entirely. We further request the Lord of the Heavenly Wilds of the Earth’s End Palace, with one hundred and twenty officials and generals, to descend and benefit the fields and labor, ensuring that roebucks, deer, birds, insects, rats, and all creatures may not inflict harm. We also beseech the Three Qi Lords of Yang Primacy, with one hundred and twenty officials and generals, to govern the Yellow Cloud Palace and seize the spirits of birds and beasts that violently damage the essence of grains and crops, preventing them from causing harm.

May the August Dao of the Void Sovereign, the local deities of the land, mountains, and forests, the Chief of Meng, the Twelve Stream Maidens, and the Lords of the Altars of Soil and Grain command that our fields yield double harvests, free from further calamity and loss. On the day our prayers are fulfilled, we shall not fail in demonstrating efficacy and trust.

We implore [Your boundless mercy].

The Most High shall discern. So forth.

Respectfully, on such-and-such a day, we submit this memorial in worship, supplicating the Heavenly Officials: for this spring’s fieldwork, may the calamities of locusts and rats be entrusted to the qi of the Dao, that we may obtain protection. One precious memorial shall be presented to the Three Heavenly Bureaus, awaiting their decree and response.

We, your servants, in utmost reverence and awe, bow our heads in prostration to make this known.

**Memorial for the Eradication of Rat Calamities**
[Ritual positions duly arranged, memorial presented as follows:]

In accordance with the sacred writ, we, your servant [Name] and disciples, have long been humble tillers of the soil, our livelihood dependent on the fields, our descendants bound to the crops. For a thousand generations, we have been fortunate to serve the Great Dao, granted the honor of wearing the exalted registers, and bestowed with manifest offices of governance. The heavenly officials, clerks, and soldiers have been our defense. Yet our sins accumulate like mountains and seas, while our merits are thinner than a hair’s breadth. In repaying Heaven and Earth, we dare not rest at ease.

In our fields, rat calamities have wrought indiscriminate harm, beyond all restraint. Unable to bear the sight, we prostrate ourselves and submit this memorial, beseeching the Most High Dao, the Venerable Lords, the Three Master Lords, the Ladies, and the Heavenly Administrators to deign in their mercy to examine our plea.

We humbly supplicate the Three-Five Lords of Yang Primacy, with one hundred and twenty officials and generals, to govern the Yellow Cloud Palace. We further implore the White Tiger General of the Southern Mountains and his officers and soldiers to descend as one, capturing the field rats within our borders and driving them back to the wilderness, forbidding them to linger in grain-bearing lands.

May the local deities of our district—the Chief of Meng, the Twelve Stream Maidens, the Lords of the Altars of Soil and Grain, and the deities of the land, mountains, and forests—join in eradicating the scourge of rats, pacifying and extinguishing them in due time. Thus shall the five grains flourish abundantly, and the people rejoice in renewal, bearing the grace of the Dao’s life-nurturing virtue.

We shall not fail in demonstrating efficacy and trust. We implore the Most High to discern.

A Memorial for the Removal of Tiger Calamities

Duly occupying our ritual station, we humbly submit this memorial:

According to the documents, we, born of womb and kin to the subordinate officers and descendants, have been blessed across a thousand generations to encounter the Great Transformation. We have received profound grace, long upheld the master’s Dao, and been bestowed the Celestial Master’s talismans and registers for our own protection. Such favor and radiance are truly excessive.

Yet now we face inauspicious calamity: tigers and wolves have entered our borders, devouring living people and harming the six livestock. Their ravages grow daily deeper, with no means to restrain them. We fear that the lives of our household—men and women—may fall into decline and adversity, ensnared in karmic nets, transgressing the manifold prohibitions: the Generals of the Great Year, the Year of Birth, the Life Destiny, the Twelve Taboos, the *fēishī* corpse-qi, the ghosts of drink and food, the mountain spirits and sea numina, the one hundred twenty spectral demons, and all those since the Most Ancient—such as the Generals of Inversion, the Generals of the Way, each invoking their official titles—along with the spirits of harm from the Five Directions and those who obstruct the roads. We beseech that none of these bring us affliction.

We implore the Northern Mysterious Lord, with one hundred twenty officers and generals, to govern the Black Bureau. We further implore the Northern Pacifying Guardian Lord, with one hundred twenty officers and generals, to govern the Red Bureau. Together may they descend, sealing our dwelling and precincts. May the true officials infuse their qi, overseeing and summoning the lords of mountains, rivers, altars of soil and grain, and local deities, that they may unite in purpose to dispel the harm of tigers and wolves.

We further implore the Lord of the Hundred Spirits in the Hidden Palace, with one hundred twenty officers and generals, to descend as one, seizing the essences of the hundred aged qi that bring misfortune to people. We implore the Earth-Restraining Lord, with one hundred twenty officers and generals, the Celestial Supervisor, the River Earl, the Water Thearch, and the Twelve Scribes, to capture and restrain the tigers and wolves of the Five Directions that slaughter all beings, along with the one hundred twenty blood-stained ghosts of harm, severing the qi of death and injury both within and without.

We implore the Lords of the Nine Yi, Eight Man, Six Rong, Five Di, and Three Qin, each according to their directional stations, in spring, summer, autumn, and winter, to join with the Three Generals of our household, the twenty-four officers, and three hundred thousand soldiers, diligently guarding and protecting. May all sentient beings be swept away. We pray that in our prefecture and county, our household—men and women, young and old—along with our oxen, horses, and six livestock, in all our comings and goings, may not encounter the calamities of tigers, wolves, and manifold disasters. May no poisonous harm cross this border, and may all receive complete protection.

May the generals, officers, and soldiers who demonstrate their efficacy be rewarded for their merit and labor. We shall not fail in demonstrating efficacy and trust. We implore the Most High to discern.

With utmost reverence, we perform the rite to expel malevolent beasts and present this memorial, submitting it to the Celestial Bureau of [Name]. Thus concluded.

**Memorial for the Dissolution of Curses and Hexes**
Duly inscribed with the proper ritual titles, we humbly address:

In accordance with the sacred writ, [Name] today declares in person: by a thousand-year fortune, I have been granted the honor of serving the Great Dao. Yet, being of humble and unworthy nature, my faith has often faltered, inviting the accumulation of baleful qi. Of late, my dwelling has been beset by misfortune; dreams assail me in confusion, and omens of ill portend without cease. My limbs grow heavy, my complexion withers, my spirit scatters, no longer bound to my form. Divination and inquiry reveal the presence of wicked persons who, through mutual malediction, invoke heaven and earth, summon ghosts and spirits, and employ a hundred forms of curses. Some inscribe my name, others craft effigies in my likeness; some pierce hearts with blades, others sever hair and fingers, offering them to the spirits of the land. I fear the hundred oath-bound ghosts now seize and detain me. I know not what merit may dissolve this, nor how to guard my life and body. With a sincere heart and offerings of utmost faith, I rely upon the Great Dao, beseeching the celestial ministers to receive my plea. I beg for this memorial to reverse and dissolve the curses.

Prostrate, I present this memorial to the Celestial Bureau, praying that the Most High Lord Lao, the Most High Venerable One, the Three Master Lords, the Ladies, and the Attendant Scribes of the Gate deign to attend, examine, and act. If the curses and hexes were cast in the spring months of yin, mao, and chen against my person, I invoke the Lords of the Nine Yi of the East, Jia and Yi, to reverse and dissolve them. If cast in the summer months of si, wu, and wei, I invoke the Lords of the Eight Man of the South, Bing and Ding, to reverse and dissolve them. If cast in the autumn months of shen, you, and xu, I invoke the Lords of the Six Rong of the West, Geng and Xin, to reverse and dissolve them. If cast in the winter months of hai, zi, and chou, I invoke the Lords of the Five Di of the North, Ren and Gui, to reverse and dissolve them. If cast in the intercalary months, may the Lords of the Three Qin of the Center, Wu and Ji, dispel and dissolve them. If the curses were cast under the twenty-eight constellations, may the Lords of the corresponding stellar lodges reverse and dissolve them. If wicked persons have crafted effigies or pierced hearts with blades, or if the curses were placed at roadside shrines, altars, prisons, sacred trees, well spirits, hearth deities, or in the domains of the River Earls, water officials, or the private spirits of heretical masters, we humbly note: the Most High is pure and exalted, the Three Heavens vast and distant, the upright qi eternal, while the perverse qi runs rampant, wrongfully harming the innocent—of whom I am but one. I fear that, unjustly ensnared, I may suddenly be claimed by the ghostly officials. I beseech the Great Dao of the Most High, Lord Lao, the Venerable One, the Heavenly Masters, the Lady Masters, the Three Master Lords, the Ladies, the Attendant Scribes, and the True Lords of the Five Qi to attend and consider. If I have transgressed the Five Oaths or the Seven Curses, I implore the million soldiers of the Supreme Prime and the hundred thousand soldiers of the Lords of Reversal to descend as one. For my sake, release the three hun and seven po, that they may not be detained; restore my hun and restrain my po, harmonizing my spirit and qi. Dissolve the thousand evils and ten thousand ghosts within my body, that they may never again disturb me. May all malevolent spirits and curses be utterly swept away. May the celestial officials I have invoked act in accordance with my words, rewarding merit and promotion. I entreat that the efficacy of this rite be manifest in my dwelling, as a sign of trust and favor. We implore the Most High to discern. Thus concluded.

May the Most High discern and distinguish. *Thus concluded.*

**Petition for the Dissolution of Malevolent Manifestations**

Having assumed the proper ritual position, I humbly submit this memorial:

In accordance with the sacred writ, I, [Name], do this day declare in my own words: born of the womb, a descendant of the lower officials and their progeny, I have been blessed across a thousand generations to serve the Great Dao. From of old, I have received boundless grace, my sincerity unceasing.

Yet of late, my dwelling has known no peace; malevolent spirits stir and disturb, and wherever I turn, misfortune prevails, with inauspicious omens appearing in succession. On this day, I suddenly beheld a manifestation of [describe] hue, which unfolded script and inscribed characters, filling me with no small distress.

I beseech the granting of one *Petition for the Dissolution of a Hundred Malevolent Manifestations*, humbly imploring its transmission to the Three Heavenly Bureaus.

In accordance with the ritual statutes, I, your disciple [Name], having investigated the ominous portents afflicting my household, now submit this petition. By the prescribed method, I offer one hundred and twenty feet of *mang* rope, a blade, and the five directional ritual pledges—coin, rice, and *ming* silk—along with one *Petition for the Dissolution of Malevolent Manifestations in the Five Directions*, reverently presented. May the Most High and Boundless Dao, the Three Masters, and the host of sages deign to bestow their compassionate regard.

I humbly aver:
In the East, the azure malevolence styles itself the Year Star, wantonly conjuring baleful manifestations. The essence of ancient trees, it stirs and manifests as green objects, inflicting widespread harm. I beseech the Azure Emperor of the East to dissolve and annihilate this malevolent calamity.

In the South, the crimson malevolence styles itself Mars, stirring and manifesting as red objects, seeking to inflict harm. May the Vermilion Emperor of the South dissolve and annihilate this malevolent calamity.

In the West, the white malevolence styles itself Venus, stirring and manifesting as white objects, intent on rebellion and treachery, wantonly producing strange anomalies. I beseech the White Emperor of the West to dissolve and annihilate this malevolent calamity.

In the North, the black malevolence styles itself Mercury, the essence of spring sources and tortoises, stirring and manifesting as black objects, altering names and forms. I beseech the Black Emperor of the North to dissolve and annihilate this malevolent manifestation.

In the Center, the yellow malevolence styles itself Saturn, stirring and manifesting as yellow objects, falsely claiming kinship, summoning inauspicious forces, and conjuring manifold anomalies. I beseech the Yellow Emperor of the Center to eradicate and annihilate this malevolent calamity.

In accordance with the *Petition of the Celestial Master to the One Thousand Two Hundred Officials*, I hereby memorialize and invoke:
- The Lord of Heavenly Prosperity, with one hundred thousand yellow-robed soldiers;
- The Lord Supervisor, with one million soldiers;
- Five Lords of the Supreme Prime, each attended by one hundred and twenty officers.

May they descend to my household to apprehend and seize the one hundred and twenty malevolent manifestations, sweeping them away in a single stroke, dissolving and annihilating them. May the essences of the ancient ones and all past transgressions be graciously pardoned and absolved.

May the celestial officials I have invoked act in accordance with the words of the Three Assemblies, rewarding merit without fail. I implore the Most High to discern. *Thus concluded.*

Petitioning for the Five Directions’ Great Petition to Dissolve Malevolent Manifestations, submitted to the Celestial Bureau:

To dispel calamity, avert misfortune, prolong life, deliver destiny, and repel slaughter—thus the memorial is presented.

In accordance with the scriptures, I, your humble servant, now declare in my own words: Born of the womb, a descendant of the lower officials’ lineage, I have been blessed across a thousand generations to serve the Great Dao and have long received its grace. Yet in this present year, upon reckoning my fate, I find disasters and adversities manifold, lacking the fortune to sustain myself. Relying solely upon my sincerity, I beseech through this petition to deliver myself and attain peace in my dwelling.

I humbly implore the Three Luminaries’ Perfected Officials to resolve and dissolve the celestial nets and earthly snares of this year, the wandering red rats of the city walls, the three mounds and five graves, the baleful stars of punishment and slaughter—all poised to bring misfortune. May they turn and shield my life, extending my years, dissolving disasters, and delivering me from adversity.

I reverently present *The Petition for Protection*, to be heard by the celestial officials of the Heavenly Bureau. May they spread and infuse the qi of the Dao into my body. I invoke:
- The Five Perfected Lords of Supreme Harmony and Love of Life,
- The Five Lords of Qi Circulation,
- The Five Lords of Deliverance from Punishment and Adversity,
- The Five Lords of Life Extension and Year Augmentation,
- The Five Lords of Life Preservation and Destiny Protection,
- The Venerable Lord of Myriad Blessings,
- The Lord of Heavenly Prosperity within the Celestial Palace, with one hundred thousand yellow-robed soldiers.

I further invoke:
- The Five Lords of Punishment Collection and Slaughter Repulsion,
- The Five Lords of Execution and Slaughter Severance,
- The Five Lords of Punishment Enforcement and Slaughter Seizure,
each attended by one hundred and twenty officers, to safeguard my body from the hundred malevolent punishments and adversities. From the first adversity to the ninth, may all be delivered, turning death into rebirth, dissolving disasters, dispersing misfortune, and transforming ill fortune into good.

Additionally, for the perils of:
- Robbery Slaughter, Calamity Slaughter, Heavenly Slaughter, Earthly Slaughter,
- Year Slaughter, Month Slaughter, Day Slaughter, Hour Slaughter,
- Yin Slaughter, Yang Slaughter, the Three Slaughters of Baleful Stars, the Five Punishments, and the Six Livestock,
all poised to bring malevolent afflictions, I invoke:
- The Five Lords of Myriad Blessings,
- The Five Lords of Qi Circulation,
- The Five Lords of Adversity Dissolution,
- The Southern Director of Destiny,
- The Radiant Star Lord of Venus,
- The Lords of Soul Restraint and Spirit Control,
- The Lords of Wealth and Prosperity,
- The Lords of Destiny’s Jade Register,
each attended by one hundred and twenty officers, to strike my name from the Register of Death and inscribe it in the Register of Life.

In accordance with the Mysterious Statutes, I offer as ritual payment:
- one bolt of plain silk,
- one thousand two hundred coins,
- one *dou* and two *sheng* of oil,
- one *shi* and two *dou* of rice,
- paper, brushes, incense, and fruit,
presented to the Ten Directions’ Numinous Officials. May they repel and expel demonic forces, nurture and protect my life, and may the Celestial Officials and Holy Mothers universally grant their favor.

I further earnestly invoke:
- The Lords of the Nine Yi of the East, with eighty-one officials,
- The Lords of the Yin, Mao, Chen, Jia, and Yi directions,
to dissolve for me the green disasters, green adversities, green pestilences, green poisons, green convulsions, and green slaughters of the East.

- The Lords of the Eight Man of the South, with sixty-four officials,
- The Lords of the Si, Wu, Wei, Bing, and Ding directions,
to dissolve for me the red disasters, red adversities, red pestilences, red poisons, red convulsions, and red slaughters of the South.

- The Lords of the Six Rong of the West, with thirty-six officials,
- The Lords of the Shen, You, Xu, Geng, and Xin directions,
to dissolve for me the white disasters, white adversities, white pestilences, white poisons, white convulsions, and white slaughters of the West.

- The Lords of the Five Di of the North, with twenty-five officials,
- The Lords of the Hai, Zi, Chou, Ren, and Gui directions,
to dissolve for me the black disasters, black adversities, black pestilences, black poisons, black inflictions, and black slaughters of the North.

- The Lords of the Three Qin of the Center, with one thousand two hundred officials,
to dissolve for me the yellow disasters, yellow adversities, yellow pestilences, yellow poisons, yellow convulsions, and yellow slaughters of the Center. May they expel the ghosts of the five directions’ yellow diseases, the seasonal miasmas, and the disasters of water and fire, dissolving them all.

May the local earth gods and village deities unite in strength to guard and protect my household, bringing daily renewal of fortune and prosperity, and clarity in both public and private affairs, fulfilling the covenant without fail.

I humbly present *The Petition to Avert Disaster, Deliver Destiny, and Uphold Unity to Pity and Deliver from Adversity*, submitted to the Celestial Bureau.

---

**Petition of Gratitude and Atonement for One’s Destiny**

In accordance with the ritual rank, I declare: Born of the womb, a descendant of the lower officials’ lineage, I have been favored across a thousand generations to serve the Orthodox Unity, entering the gates of the Dao. By the grace of my teachers and elders, I have received honors, been granted talismans and registers for self-discipline, advanced to the Middle Vehicle, and borne the weight of their trust. Entrusted with the office of governance, I have upheld the scriptures and treasures of the Dao. The boundless grace of such favor is beyond measure.

Yet I, your servant, am dull-witted, my spirit and qi unsettled, my three *hun* souls unguarded, my seven *po* souls restless. In utmost reverence and fear, I bow my head and prostrate myself before the August Jade Emperor.

I and my seven generations of ancestors have committed hidden sins and manifest transgressions, accumulating the guilt of killing and harming living beings, all recorded by the Three Officials. From this day forward, I beseech that my ten thousand transgressions be dissolved, my sins erased, malevolent qi annihilated, and the nine blessings perpetually secure. May the souls of my seven generations of ancestors, down to my distant descendants, ascend and be reborn, returning to the womb as infants.

May I, your servant, attain the longevity of the immortals, eternal life in the Great Void, and bow to the Jade Purity of the North.

In utmost reverence and fear, I bow my head and prostrate myself before the Three Primordial Lords of the Great Simplicity.

I and my seven generations of ancestors, down to myself, have committed hidden sins and manifest transgressions, the guilt of killing living beings, all recorded before the Emperor. From this day forward, I beseech that my sins be erased, death struck from the records and life inscribed, my ten thousand transgressions dissolved. May my seven generations of ancestors return to the Jade Court, ascend to the sun and moon, and wander among the seven stars.

I, your servant, bow my head and prostrate myself before the Three Pure Ones of the Supreme Clarity.

Since the dawn of my awareness, I have committed a thousand sins and ten thousand transgressions, extending to the hidden evils of my seven generations of ancestors, all recorded by the Three Officials. From this day forward, I beseech that my ten thousand sins be dissolved, deceit and malevolence eradicated, hidden sins scattered, my seven generations of ancestors restored to spirit, my body ascend to the Emperor’s Hall, and my path return to the Jade Court.

I, your servant, in utmost reverence and awe, bow my head and prostrate myself before the Four Elder Lords of the Dao-Middle.

Since seven generations past, extending to my seven generations of ancestors, the hidden rebellions and accumulated evils we have committed—all recorded by the Three Yin Officials—I beseech that from this day forward, my thousand sins be scattered and dissolved, my ten thousand transgressions overturned and erased, my hun and po souls made distinct, my seven generations of ancestors returned to the womb of rebirth, the ten thousand spirits attend as guardians, the Five Elders establish my talisman, my lifespan equal that of Heaven and Earth, and my name and form inscribed in the Jade Register.

I, your servant, in utmost reverence and awe, bow my head and prostrate myself before the Three Bureau Lords.

May from this day onward, the knots of my sins be untangled and dispersed, the qi of my transgressions vanish, the hundred evils never arise, perverse qi be concealed and severed, my seven generations of ancestors ascend as immortals, my three hun souls harmonized and refined, my seven po souls bound in purity, and the multitude of spirits support and attend me, that I may become an Upper Perfected.

I, your servant, in utmost reverence and awe, bow my head and prostrate myself.

Within are seven sections of similar wording, which are not transcribed here, as the original submission is thus.

I, your humble servant, born in this thousand-year turning of the cosmic wheel, have been permitted to dwell at the end of the Dao and, though unworthy, have received the office of governance. Yet I am dull-witted, raised in the common stream, my offenses piled high as mountains and seas, with no self-awareness. Clinging to life and desiring its pleasures, I rise early and retire late, never settling my breath.

I humbly implore the transforming grace of the Most High, whose beneficence extends without limit, to embrace even the foolish among the people, and to bestow the method of dissolving sins. Though my person is lowly and my Dao shallow, I dare to approach the pure and solemn, presenting this memorial in gratitude. My five emotions tremble in awe, my liver and heart feel rent asunder.

I specially beseech the Dao Lord to grant the mercy of the Three Pardons, to take pity on my earnest sincerity, and further to bestow the daily renewal of Dao-qi, that all I attain may flow unimpeded, every endeavor succeed as my heart desires, my household flourish, and all within—great and small—receive your grace, as a token of my devotion.

May the Most High Great Dao Lord deign to consider this.

---

Such being the case, and with the collective endorsement of the assembled officials, your servant reverently bows and presents this memorial to the Great Dao of the Three Heavens, humbly expressing gratitude for the years of this body’s existence. For seven generations past, and for the Three Masters of this present life, for parents living and deceased, for hidden sins and manifest transgressions, I beseech the gift of long life and the eternal preservation of the Water of Life.

One memorial is herewith respectfully submitted, to be conveyed to the Three Heavenly Courts of the Most High, prostrating in reverence to make this known. The *Feidu Jiu’e Tianluo Zhang* is presented in full accordance with its ritual rank, and the memorial states as follows:

At such-and-such a palace lies the severance of fate; at such-and-such a palace, the destiny of this life; and on such-and-such a taboo day in such-and-such a month and year, there is fear of entanglement in the celestial net, of encirclement by the earthly snare—only terror is known, no distinction made. With undivided devotion, I rely upon the ritual codes of the Heavenly Master of the Great Dao and, on behalf of the Li family, reverently present the *Feidu Jiu’e Tianluo Zhang*. I have prepared one hundred twenty feet of blue silk, one hundred twenty counting rods, one *shi* and two *dou* of life-bestowing rice, one bolt of plain silk, one thousand two hundred coins, and incense, oil, paper, and brushes, all to petition for the *Zhang* of deliverance and liberation from calamities.

I humbly invoke the Lords of the Nine Yi of the East, the nine months of spring—*yin*, *mao*, *chen*, *jia*, *yi*—and the eighty-one official lords of the Nine Nines; the Lords of the Eight Man of the South, the three months of summer—*si*, *wu*, *wei*, *bing*, *ding*—and the sixty-four official lords of the Eight Eights; the Lords of the Six Rong of the West, the three months of autumn—*shen*, *you*, *xu*, *geng*, *xin*—and the thirty-six official lords of the Six Sixes; the Lords of the Five Di of the North, the three months of winter—*hai*, *zi*, *chou*, *ren*, *gui*—and the twenty-five official lords of the Five Fives. May each deign to descend to the altar, unite in purpose and strength, and eradicate the calamities of this household.

I further invoke the Great General of Life Extension, with one thousand two hundred soldiers, to descend as one and, for the disciples—both male and female—prolong their years, support them through decline and adversity, eternally safeguard their primordial auspiciousness, and ensure the year’s end without misfortune, as a token of devotion.

May the grace of the Most High—

The Most High makes distinctions. Thus it is said. For [the petitioner], unbind the calamities and peril, and ascend through the Nine Perils of the Celestial Net, presenting one chapter of the *Feidu Jiu’e Tianluo*. It is submitted to the [Petitioner’s] Court with a single summons of stone.

The *Que Sanzai* chapter is presented in full ritual position, and the memorial states: Thus it is said. Since the [specified] month and day, [the petitioner] has been afflicted with illness and suffering. Thus it is said. Upon the master’s examination, it is found that the year and fate are inauspicious. Within the reckoning of the Nine Palaces and the flying tally of the *yuanchen* calendar, there is a convergence of opposing calculations, now exhausted. Moreover, both public and private matters, disputes and slander, water and fire, tigers and wolves, insects and serpents—all manifold perils—cling to the body. Some are this year’s *jiesha*, others next year’s *zaisha*; some are the *niansha*, *yuesha*, *risha*, or *shisha*, or the *yinchen* killer. There are the Five Directions’ slayers: the Green Slayer of the East, the Red Slayer of the South, the White Slayer of the West, the Black Slayer of the North, and the Yellow Slayer of the Center. One also fears entanglement in the Celestial Net and Earthly Web, dreading sudden harm without escape, causing great and small to tremble in terror, with no recourse.

Thus, considering the Nine Perils of the year—first, second, third, fourth, fifth, sixth, seventh, eighth, and ninth—the perils of tigers, wolves, blades, and weapons; the perils of bandits and corvée; the perils of the Three Punishments and Three Slayers—I now invoke the Lord of Deliverance from Peril, the Lord of Life’s Stability, the Lord of Longevity, the Lord of Life’s Augmentation, the Lord of Life’s Continuance, the Lord of Deliverance and Life Extension, and the Lord of Great Fortune and Virtue. Each is accompanied by one hundred twenty officials and generals.

I further invoke the August Heavenly Thearch, the Canopy of Sun and Moon, the Lords of the Northern Dipper, the Three Heavens’ Record-Keeping Lords of Fate, and the Marshal of Deliverance from Peril. Together with the directly attending Merit Officers, they descend to govern the hundred illnesses within [the petitioner’s] abdomen. The Orthodox Unity Merit Officer descends to govern the hundred illnesses within the heart. The Illness-Treating Merit Officer descends to govern the hundred illnesses within the spleen. The *Qi*-Directing Merit Officer descends to govern the hundred illnesses within the stomach. The Central Region Merit Officer descends to govern the hundred illnesses within the liver. The Yang Spirit Deciding Clerk descends to govern the hundred illnesses beneath the left armpit. The Yin Spirit Deciding Clerk descends to govern the hundred illnesses beneath the right armpit. The Wolf and Tiger Guards descend to govern the hundred illnesses within the intestines. The Inspector of Treachery descends to govern the hundred illnesses within the lungs. The Hook-Riding Lord descends to govern the hundred illnesses within the lower abdomen. The Three Officials’ Archers descend to govern the hundred illnesses within the back and spine. The Celestial Armored Soldiers descend to govern the hundred illnesses within the twenty fingers. The Celestial *Ding* Warriors descend to govern the hundred illnesses within the head and brain.

May all these maladies be eradicated and cured.

General Wang Wenqing of *Jiazi*, leading thirty-six thousand soldiers, stands guard to the left and right, defending until *you*. General Zhan Zijiang of *Jiaxu*, leading thirty-six thousand soldiers, stands guard to the left and right, defending until *wei*. General Hu Wenchang of *Jiashen*, leading twenty-six thousand soldiers, stands guard to the left and right, defending until *si*. General Wei Shangqing of *Jiawu*, leading thirty-six thousand soldiers, stands guard to the left and right, defending until *mao*. General Meng Feiqing of *Jiachen*, leading thirty-six thousand soldiers, stands guard to the left and right, defending until *chou*. General Ming Wenzhang of *Jiayin*, leading thirty-six thousand soldiers, stands guard to the left and right, defending until *hai*.

The Six *Jia* Generals, with their six divisions of troops, each leading thirty-six thousand soldiers, transmit and coordinate in timely succession, following the petitioner’s body through east and west, south and north, in motion and stillness. True spirits provide protection, standing guard and defending, dissolving the petitioner’s calamities and perils, repelling and extinguishing pestilent *qi*, prolonging the years of life, ensuring the household’s peace and prosperity, and granting repose to kin and dependents—all by the vast virtue of the Great Dao.

The celestial officials and laboring lords, having deigned to descend, shall on the three auspicious assembly days of the year have their merits memorialized in full. They shall be promoted in rank, their emoluments increased, and their rewards elevated, in fulfillment of this pledge of devotion.

Invoking the boundless grace of the Most High,

A petition for deliverance from illness, calamity, and mortal peril—one document—is hereby submitted to the celestial bureaus.

A writ of exorcism, inscribed on azure silk with the remnants of sacred script, is presented in proper ritual form, proclaiming: From birth, this petitioner, a descendant of the earthly officials and a child of posterity, has been blessed across a thousand generations.

Yet of late, misfortune has clung to this body, and in this year of advancing fate, the petitioner humbly offers precious tokens of faith: forty feet of white silk to secure deliverance from calamity; one *shi* and two *dou* of rice to double provisions and augment life’s allotment, filling the granary’s measures; one thousand two hundred *wen* in coin to attest sincerity, stabilizing the three hundred sixty spirits and *qi*, ensuring their palaces grow daily more secure.

Brush, ink, paper, and counting rods record the petitioner’s name for rebirth. Five effigies are cast to ascend in the petitioner’s stead to the five directions, transforming form and altering name. Fragrant oil and lamps maintain unbroken illumination. These offerings of rice and coin serve as pledges of sincerity, redeeming and ransoming this life.

The petitioner now invokes: twelve Lords of Deliverance from the Most High’s palace; twelve Lords of Life Extension; five Maidens of the Tripod Granary; five Lords of Destiny; one thousand two hundred Jade Maidens of the Five Planetary Palaces; one Lord of the Hall of Light; one Lord of Southern Prosperity; one Lord of Vermilion Yang; one Lord of the Yellow and the Old; one Lord of the Celestial Soul and one of the Earthly Spirit; one thousand two hundred Maidens of Revitalization; one thousand two hundred Maidens of the Jade Calendar; one hundred twenty officials each from the celestial, terrestrial, and water bureaus; and all summoned lords and functionaries of the various offices—may they unite in purpose and strength to deliver this disciple from the trials of fate, ensuring dwelling and abode remain peaceful, stable, and free from harm.

As pledged, the merits of the invoked celestial officials shall be memorialized on the three auspicious assembly days, their ranks elevated on propitious dates, in fulfillment of this vow of devotion.

Invoking once more the boundless grace of the Most High.

**Memorial for the Treatment of Illness**

In proper ritual rank, this memorial respectfully states:

As previously reported, this disciple has recently fallen ill, fearing drowning upon the path of life. Humbly approaching this minister, I beseech a memorial be presented to the Three Celestial Bureaus, praying for deliverance and redemption.

For some ten days now, cold and heat have been unbalanced, the pores disordered. Perhaps exposed to drafts or external chill, this illness was thus contracted—or perhaps by the Five Punishments and Three Calamities, a karmic retribution. Yet in my ignorance and obstruction, I know not how to examine and remedy this.

I now invoke the generative qi of the Five Directions to aid in healing. With special reverence, I beseech the Most High and Boundless Dao, the Most High Lord Lao, the Lords and Venerable Ones, the Celestial Master Lord, the Three Master Lords, the Lady, the Compassionate Father, and the Holy Mother—to bestow grace and mindfulness, granting the Dao’s qi to shield and respond to this disciple’s body.

Respectfully, I petition the Celestial Bureau, presenting to the Heavenly Physicians and the Twelve Lords of the Grand Physicians, that they descend to this disciple’s body and, wherever the illness resides, administer healing. I invoke the Fifteen Merit Officers for the Treatment of Illness to beseech the Celestial Bureau, erasing the roots of this disciple’s transgressions from past and present lives. May the five viscera, the four limbs, and the hundred vessels all receive cure and recovery.

Next, I invoke the Eastern Blue Generative Qi, the Southern Red Generative Qi, the Western White Generative Qi, the Northern Black Generative Qi, and the Central Yellow Generative Qi—all to descend into this disciple’s body.

Furthermore, I invoke the Lord of Release from Tribulation, the Lord of Life-Deliverance, the Lord of Lifespan Augmentation, the Lord of People’s Protection, the Lord of Calamity’s Punishment, the Great General of the Wandering Net, and the Great General of Earthly Boundaries—each to seize evil spirits, stale qi, and plague-demons, that the afflicted may be restored to health.

The celestial officials thus invoked shall have their merits memorialized on the three auspicious assembly days, their ranks elevated on propitious dates, in fulfillment of this vow of devotion. With gratitude, I reverently distinguish the grace of the Most High.

**Petition for the Eradication of Disease, Expulsion of Calamitous Evil, and Protection of Life**

In due observance of ritual protocol, this memorial is respectfully submitted:

Whereas this disciple suffers from grave and grievous illness, I humbly submit this urgent petition, beseeching the submission of a memorial. For the transgressions and karmic entanglements I have incurred are profound. Relying upon the great Dao, should compassionate aid be granted, I implore that my lifespan be extended and my illness cured this very day.

With reverence, I invoke the Yin-Yang Healing Merit Officers and the Five Officials of Medicine to proceed to the Phoenix Celestial Palace, within the Solar Gate, and there procure the Five-Colored Divine Medicines of the Great Purity. May these be poured into my mouth, flowing through the hundred vessels, filling my abdomen and chest, that all chronic ailments may dissolve and heal.

The Wood Official shall administer the medicine; the Fire Official shall preside over moxibustion; the Metal Official shall wield the needle; the Water Official shall prepare the decoction; the Earth Official shall harmonize the formulas—each attending to their appointed task. May the nine orifices align in harmony, the five viscera flow unimpeded, and the six bowels achieve balance.

I further invoke the Lord of Harmonious Longevity, the Lord of Supreme Harmony, the Lord of the Great Yang, the Lord of Lifespan Extension, the Lord of Life Protection, the Lord of Tribulation’s Passage, the Five Thearchs’ Elder, and the Lord of Primal Qi. Additionally, I summon the Great General of the Lofty Standard, along with three hundred thousand troops of the Reversed Armor and Inverted Scales, to descend and purge the evil spirits from my five viscera, six bowels, four limbs, joints, twelve palaces, and one hundred twenty barriers and mechanisms.

Should any evil spirits remain bound to my body, I petition the Three Officials of Heaven, Earth, and Water; the Five Marchmounts and Four Waterways; the Mountain and Forest Elders; and the Twenty-Four Taboos—all to join with the Riding Officers of the Crimson Heaven’s Fierce Wind, whom I bear upon my person, in the capture of these malevolent spirits.

Moreover, I entreat the Lord of Myriad Blessings, the Lord of the Celestial Granary, the Lord of the Eastern Blue Qi, the Lord of the Southern Red Qi, the Lord of the Western White Qi, the Lord of the Northern Black Qi, and the Lord of the Central Yellow Qi—each to lead their legions and descend into my body to expel all perverse qi.

May I be restored to health, my life prolonged, and my well-being preserved without mishap. Should this petition be fulfilled, the merits of the celestial officials thus invoked shall be memorialized on the three auspicious assembly days, their ranks elevated in due course, in fulfillment of this vow of devotion. With gratitude, I reverently distinguish the grace of the Most High.

For my afflicted body, stricken with grave illness and confined to bed, I reverently present this *Memorial for Life-Prolonging Protection*, submitting it to the [Celestial] Bureau of [N.N.]. Herein lies the *Memorial for Support in Decline and Deliverance from Calamity*, duly inscribed with its ritual rank and addressed as follows:

I, [N.N.], unworthy heir to a minor official’s lineage, was formed through the six qi and owe my existence to ten thousand kalpas of good fortune. Bathed in the radiance of the Three Luminaries, I dwell in this extraordinary age and have been granted a place among humankind. Yet this year, my misfortunes run deep, and the days stretch long; even my constancy and blessings are imperiled. I have heard that the Great Dao, in its boundless grace, rescues the common people, reviving withered bones and restoring the dead to life. Having received this immeasurable mercy, I am profoundly grateful.

Should my calamity lie within the Eastern Celestial Prison, I entreat the Azure Emperor of the East, Lord of Jia-Yi and the Nine Yi Tribes, along with his retinue of eighty-one officials, to mount the Azure Dragon, traverse ten thousand leagues, and wield their tablets and talismans to dissolve for me the azure disasters, azure calamities, azure pestilences, azure misfortunes, and azure poisons of the East. May all baleful qi of the three spring months be utterly swept away.

Should my calamity lie within the Southern Celestial Prison, I entreat the Vermilion Emperor of the South, Lord of Bing-Ding and the Eight Man Tribes, along with his retinue of sixty-four officials, to mount the Vermilion Dragon, traverse ten thousand leagues, and wield their tablets and talismans to dissolve for me the vermilion disasters, vermilion calamities, vermilion pestilences, vermilion misfortunes, and vermilion poisons of the South. May all baleful qi of the three summer months be utterly swept away.

Should my calamity lie within the Western Celestial Prison, I entreat the White Emperor of the West, Lord of Geng-Xin and the Six Rong Tribes, along with his retinue of thirty-six officials, to mount the White Dragon, traverse ten thousand leagues, and wield their tablets and talismans to dissolve for me the white disasters, white calamities, white pestilences, white misfortunes, and white poisons of the West. May all baleful qi of the three autumn months be utterly swept away.

Should my calamity lie within the Northern Celestial Prison, I entreat the Black Emperor of the North, Lord of Ren-Gui and the Five Di Tribes, along with his retinue of twenty-five officials, to mount the Black Dragon, traverse ten thousand leagues, and wield their tablets and talismans to dissolve for me the black disasters, black calamities, black pestilences, black misfortunes, and black poisons of the North. May all baleful qi of the three winter months be utterly swept away.

Should my calamity lie within the Central Celestial Prison, I entreat the Yellow Emperor of the Center, Lord of Wu-Ji and the Three Qin Tribes, along with his retinue of nine thousand two hundred officials, to mount the Yellow Dragon, traverse ten thousand leagues, and wield their tablets and talismans to dissolve for me the yellow disasters, yellow calamities, yellow pestilences, yellow misfortunes, and yellow poisons of the Center. May all calamities from the first to the ninth, and all eight adversities afflicting my body, be dispelled.

Furthermore, I entreat the August Heavenly Thearch, the Sun and Moon and Five Planets, the Five Thearchs and their Ministers, the Lord of the Canopy and Northern Dipper, and the Lords of the Three Heavens’ Registers and Life-Commands to descend as one and dissolve for me the three disasters and nine calamities, as well as this year’s pestilential miasmas and jaundiced vapors, driving them far from body and mind.

Today, I offer in devotion: one bolt of white silk, one *shi* and two *dou* of rice, one thousand two hundred cash coins, twelve *sheng* of oil, and incense, lamps, paper, and brushes as tokens of my sincerity. By this offering, I pledge my unwavering faith.

I reverently petition the Most High of the Three Heavens to erase my name from the Register of the Dead and inscribe it in the Register of the Living, excising all afflictions of the myriad illnesses. May my household enjoy peace, may the Dao’s power sustain me, and may my office and salary be advanced. On the day this grace is bestowed, may the celestial officials and their legions, in accordance with the three auspicious assembly days, be duly rewarded for their merits, and may this vow of devotion not be in vain.

With gratitude, I reverently distinguish the grace of the Most High.

I prostrate and present one memorial, the *Petition to the Celestial Officials for Support in Declining Years and Deliverance from Calamity*, to be conveyed to the respective bureaus. The *Memorial of Gratitude to the Earth Deities* is hereby submitted, detailing the following:

Of late, my dwelling has been inauspicious, attracting misfortune and adversity. Within this residence, the earth spirits and local deities have pursued and held me accountable. I know not what meritorious deeds to perform to safeguard my household. With wholehearted devotion, I rely upon the Great Dao. I humbly beseech memorials to be presented to the Three Heavenly Bureaus, praying that the presiding officials may, in due time, review and attend to this matter.

I reverently petition the Five Lords of Gratitude to the Earth, the Five Lords of Earth Regulation, the Five Lords of Earth Appeasement, the Five Lords of Earth Stabilization, and the Five Lords of Dwelling Pacification, along with their one hundred twenty attendant officers, to collectively descend and absolve my household of offenses against the deities of the five directions and the myriad earth spirits. Since the establishment of this dwelling, whether in recent or past times, I have dug and excavated, moved fences and replaced pillars, constructed buildings, commenced earthworks, leveled high ground and filled low, altered gates and doors, transgressed the taboos of the Six Jia, disturbed the myriad spirits of tiles and stones, the hidden corpses and concealed remains, copper and iron, white earth, black earth, and yellow earth, the Earth Sovereigns and Earth Kings, the Earth Ministers and Earth Palaces, the Generals of Earth, the Earth Lords, the Lords of the Earth Below, the Two Thousand Stone Officials, the Yin Earth and Yang Earth, the Four Seasons and Five Phases, the Great Central Sovereign, the front and back of the dwelling, the left and right of the dwelling, the Five Earth Spirit Kings, the Directors of the Central Courtyard, the Gate-Attending Gentlemen, the Gate Sergeants and Door Guards, the spirits of wells and privies, the Azure Dragon and White Tiger, the Vermilion Bird and Dark Warrior, the Soaring Serpent and Hidden Dragon, the Year Star, the Grand Yin, the Grand Yang, the Director of Destiny, the officers of the twelve hours, the Celestial Rigidity and Grand Unity, the Victorious and Lesser Auspices, the Conveying and Following Chief, the River Chief, the Ascending Clarity and Divine Successor, the Great Auspice and Merit Clerk, the Grand Assault, the Restraining Punishment, the Breaking and Killing spirits within the earth, the true numina of the four first months, four middle months, and four last months, the *zi*, *wu*, *mao*, and *you* hours, the Gate of Heaven and Door of Earth.

For offenses against the earth deities of the eastern direction, absolution is sought at the *Zhen* Palace. For offenses against the earth deities of the southern direction, absolution is sought at the *Li* Palace.

For offenses against the earth deities of the western direction, absolution is sought at the *Dui* Palace. For offenses against the earth deities of the northern direction, absolution is sought at the *Kan* Palace. For offenses against the earth deities of the central direction, absolution is sought at the *Qian*, *Kun*, *Gen*, and *Xun* Palaces, and all are granted pardon and amnesty.

O Guardian Deities of this dwelling, Yanzi and Dai the Great, with threefold roofing and threefold shelter from rain, to the east, west, south, and north, may all perverse spirits, lingering *qi*, and every misfortune and harm be swept away at once. May this household, young and old, forever enjoy primordial auspiciousness.

We humbly beseech the Most High to discern and distinguish. We implore mercy.

Since the construction of this dwelling, we have unwittingly transgressed against the dwelling deities and the earth lords’ prohibitions, incurring mutual pursuit and reproach. We reverently present this petition of absolution and expiation, one document, to ascend to the Three Heavenly Bureaus.

**Petition to Dispel Depleting Ghosts**
Duly recording the ritual rank,
From the High Antiquity: ...

Yet in this household, quarrels arise without cause, and servants flee or rebel, all due to the depletion and haunting of malevolent ghosts. We earnestly invoke the Five-Fortune Celestial Officials, the Twelve Earthly Deities and their officers, and the one hundred twenty attendants to investigate this petition and submit it on our behalf. May they capture and restore the five-depletion and six-depletion ghosts within this dwelling, returning each to their proper direction.

The green-depletion and green-depletion ghosts are to be sent to the Eastern Green Emperor for confinement, forbidden to wander. The red-depletion and red-depletion ghosts are to be sent to the Southern Red Emperor for confinement, forbidden to wander. The white-depletion and white-depletion ghosts are to be sent to the Western White Emperor for confinement, forbidden to wander. The black-depletion and black-depletion ghosts are to be sent to the Northern Black Emperor for confinement, forbidden to wander. The yellow-depletion and yellow-depletion ghosts are to be sent to the Central Yellow Emperor for confinement, forbidden to wander, that they may no longer disturb this household.

May the invoked celestial officials and soldiers, along with the Three Generals guarding this dwelling and their three hundred thousand troops, unite in purpose and strength to expel the depleting ghosts from this dwelling. May this household’s wealth and property gather and flourish, misfortune be transformed into fortune, silkworms and fields yield a hundredfold, cattle and calves fill the pens, gold and silver accumulate, quarrels cease, disasters vanish, all wishes be fulfilled, the household thrive in peace, and wealth and sustenance increase.

**Petition for Dwelling Pacification**
Duly recording the ritual rank,

**Petition to the Celestial Court:**

We, the undersigned [number] persons, humbly submit: our dwelling has been unsettled, and we fear we have unwittingly offended the netherworld authorities, thereby inviting the influx of baleful *qi*. In this year’s celestial cycle, the Five Poisons spread unchecked, afflicting the people of heaven without regard for the virtuous or the base.

We, born of the womb in ignorance, descendants of the lower officials, have by a thousand generations’ fortune been granted the grace to serve the Great Dao. Yet we remain ever fearful, finding no ground upon which to rest secure. Recently, our household—elders and children alike—has dwelt within this troubled abode, unable to safeguard ourselves, our anxieties deepening.

In recent years, we may have undertaken repairs, excavations, or renovations—moving fences, replacing pillars—matters of no single kind, yet all risking transgression against the celestial prohibitions and earthly taboos: the Generals of the Great Sun and the Grand Year-Star, the spirits of heads and feet, the *qi* of one’s ruling year and life destiny, the Great and Lesser Depletions, the baleful stars of calamity and misfortune, the Hooking Chen and White Tiger, the spirits of the twelve hours, the earthly numina and earthly slayers, all manner of depletions, and the officials of the upper and lower earth. We fear such offenses have caused the spirits of our dwelling to grow restless, and the dragon deities presiding over our well and hearth to withhold their favor. We pray that our household may be granted stability, our dwelling prosper, and all within find peace.

Invoking the *Petition of the Twelve Hundred Officials of the Celestial Master*, we reverently beseech the descent of one hundred twenty divine lords, generals, and officials, led by the *Qingyi* Great Masters, to absolve our household of all past and present transgressions and to dissolve them entirely. We humbly entreat the Five Lords of the Earth and their one hundred twenty officials to dispel the Generals of the Grand Year-Star, Great Yin, and Great Sun; the Great and Lesser Depletions; the spirits of silkworm chambers and livestock; and all ghosts bound by upper and lower prohibitions—may they be utterly eradicated.

We reverently summon:
- The Nine Lords of the Eastern Yi, under the Azure Emperor,
- The Eight Lords of the Southern Man, under the Vermilion Emperor,
- The Six Lords of the Western Rong, under the White Emperor,
- The Five Lords of the Northern Di, under the Black Emperor,
- The Three Lords of the Central Qin, under the Yellow Emperor,

along with the *qi* of the four seasons and the five earths, mutually dividing their influences, and the officials and generals of the four directions. May they descend to our dwelling to purge all prohibitions, the thousand spirits and ten thousand demons, the lingering *qi* of the lower officials, and the baleful ghosts of years, months, days, and hours—all calamities, ruptures, and harms—may they be utterly dissolved.

May the Five Emperors pacify this dwelling, and may no misfortunes arise. May blessings and protection abide through the year, the four seasons pass in tranquility, the eight solar terms remain free of disaster, and the twenty-four *qi* nodes align in harmony. May Heaven above broadly cover, and Earth below universally bear, that we may forever enjoy steadfast fortune.

- The Azure Dragon of *Zhen* governs the left of the dwelling,
- The Vermilion Dragon of *Li* governs the front,
- The White Dragon of *Dui* governs the right,
- The Black Dragon of *Kan* governs the rear,
- The Yellow Dragon of *Kun* guards the center.

May the Five Dragons govern this dwelling, repelling all inauspiciousness, dissolving all malevolence, and sweeping away a thousand woes. May the divine dragons bring peace and stability, fostering harmony among the four neighbors. May rebellion be transformed into obedience, past transgressions erased, and future goodness accomplished. May the *qi* of the Dao flow freely, rendering the dwelling pure and auspicious. May officials ascend in rank, all desires be fulfilled, and the day of heart’s contentment arrive—without fail or betrayal of trust.

We implore the Most High to discern and grant our plea. We beseech with lamentation. Thus concludes this petition.

For the household of [Certain Family], fearing that their dwelling may be unsettled, the Dragon spirits unfavorable, and taboos obstructed, I humbly present this petition. I earnestly appeal to the **Celestial Officials** and their subordinates, beseeching them to:

- Remove the malevolent *qi* of ghosts,
- Soothe the **Netherworld Officials** (*Míngsī*),
- Invite the Five Dragons to dwell and protect the premises and its occupants.

I pray for a **Precious Charter of Grace** (*Enbǎo zhāng*) to be granted and delivered to the [Certain] Bureau, thus:

---
**Charter of Plague Eradication** (*Duànwēn dúyì zhāng*)
With due respect to the **Celestial Hierarchy** (*Dàodào*), I submit:

- May the **Celestial Officials** (*Shàngguān*) command the cessation of the plague.
- Though I am dim-witted and ignorant of the malevolent *qi* of ghosts, according to the **Thousand and Two Hundred Officials’ Charter** (*Tiānshī qiān èr bǎi guān zhāng*), there exist **Lowly Officials** (*Xiàguān*) of *qi*, along with **Licentious Ghosts** and **Bandit Spirits** (*Yéyín guǐ zéi*), encircling the **Heavenly Circuit** (*Zhōutiān*) and the Earth, recklessly generating calamities and afflicting virtuous folk.
